<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 52" name="FNopinion1.52" href="#FRopinion1.52">52</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Id.,</em> at 169 (emphasis deleted).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 53" name="FNopinion1.53" href="#FRopinion1.53">53</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Id.,</em> at 160 (emphasis deleted).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 54" name="FNopinion1.54" href="#FRopinion1.54">54</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Some late 18th century and early 19th century dictionaries provided special definitions of the term "peace" as used in the law, and these definitions fit the offenses on Blackstone's list.  See, <em>e.g.</em>, 1 Johnson (6th ed. 1785) ("That general security and quiet which the king warrants to his subjects, and of which he therefore avenges the violation; every forcible injury is a breach of the king's peace" (emphasis deleted)); 5 G. Jacob, Law-Dictionary (1811) ("[P]articularly in law, ['peace'] intends a quiet behaviour towards the King and his Subjects"); Bailey (defining "peace" in the "<em>Law Sense</em>" as "quiet and inoffensive Behaviour towards King and Subject").</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 55" name="FNopinion1.55" href="#FRopinion1.55">55</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Such an interpretation would also clash with the way in which the scope of state legislative power was understood.  If any violation of the law had been regarded as a breach of public peace or safety, there would have been no need for the lawmaking authority of a state legislature to extend any further, but there is no evidence that state legislative authority was understood that way.  New York's 1777 Constitution demonstrates the point.  As noted above, it protected free exercise unless a person invoked that protection to "excuse Acts of Licentiousness, or justify Practices inconsistent with the Peace or Safety of this State."  Art. XXXVIII, in Cogan 26.  But the New York Constitution authorized the legislature to enact laws to further broader aims, including "good government, welfare, and prosperity."  Art. XIX, in 5 Federal and State Constitutions 2633 (F. Thorpe ed. 1909).  That authority obviously goes well beyond the prohibition of "Practices inconsistent with" the "Peace" and "Safety" (or "Licentiousness").  See McConnell, Freedom from Persecution 835-836.  In like manner, State Constitutions and other declarations of rights commonly proclaimed that government should pursue broader goals, such as the promotion of "prosperity" and "happiness."  See Nestor, Table III: Comparing the Provisos to the Scope of Legislative Power (online source archived at www.supremecourt.gov).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 56" name="FNopinion1.56" href="#FRopinion1.56">56</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Mayer, The Continental Army, in A Companion to the American Revolution 309 (J. Greene &amp; J. Pole eds. 2000); R. Wright, The Continental Army 153-154, 163 (1983).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 57" name="FNopinion1.57" href="#FRopinion1.57">57</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See The Oxford Companion to American Military History 606-608, 611 (J. Chambers ed. 1999).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 58" name="FNopinion1.58" href="#FRopinion1.58">58</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See Declaration of Independence  31 ("[W]e mutually pledge to each other our Lives, our Fortunes and our sacred Honor"); see also P. Maier, American Scripture 152-153 (1997); Boyd, The Declaration of Independence: The Mystery of the Lost Original, 100 Pa. Mag. Hist. &amp; Bio. 438, 445 (1976); L. Montross, The Reluctant Rebels 165 (1970); E. Burnett, The Continental Congress 196-197 (1941).  Of the 56 signers of the Declaration of Independence, 9 were taken as prisoners of war; 2 had sons who died; 3 had sons who were taken captive; 9 had their homes destroyed; and 13 saw their homes occupied, confiscated, or damaged.  M. Novak, On Two Wings: Humble Faith and Common Sense at the American Founding 157-158 (2002).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 59" name="FNopinion1.59" href="#FRopinion1.59">59</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See Barclay, The Historical Origins of Judicial Religious Exemptions, 96 Notre Dame L. Rev. 55, 69-73 (2020); McConnell, Free Exercise Revisionism 1118; Campbell, A New Approach 978, 987; Lombardi, Free Exercise 385; Campbell, Religious Neutrality in the Early Republic, 24 Regent U. L.&nbsp;Rev. 311, 314-315, n.&nbsp;20 (2012).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 60" name="FNopinion1.60" href="#FRopinion1.60">60</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;W. Newman &amp; P. Halvorson, Atlas of American Religion 18 (2000).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 61" name="FNopinion1.61" href="#FRopinion1.61">61</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Ibid.</em></p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 62" name="FNopinion1.62" href="#FRopinion1.62">62</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;The Covenanters originated in Scotland, where they opposed the Stuart kings' right to rule over the Presbyterian Church.  See Emery, Church and State in the Early Republic: The Covenanters' Radical Critique, 25 J. L. &amp; Religion 487, 488 (2009).  They immigrated to the United States and, in the 1790s, organized a branch of the Reformed Presbyterian Church.  <em>Id.,</em> at 489.  Members ascribe to two foundational documents--the Scottish National Covenant of 1638 and the Solemn League and Covenant of 1643--and believe in the supremacy of God over man in both civil and ecclesiastical matters.  <em>Id.,</em> at 448; see also J. McFeeters, The Covenanters in America: The Voice of Their Testimony on Present Moral Issues 57 (1892).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 63" name="FNopinion1.63" href="#FRopinion1.63">63</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Privileged Communications to Clergymen, 1 Cath. Law. 199, 207-209 (1955).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 64" name="FNopinion1.64" href="#FRopinion1.64">64</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See also Walsh 41; Campbell, A New Approach 992, n. 99; Lombardi,<em> </em>Free Exercise 408, and n. 152.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 65" name="FNopinion1.65" href="#FRopinion1.65">65</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See McFeeters, The Covenanters in America 121-129; <em>id.,</em> at 122 (Covenanters "must refuse upon the grounds of honor, conscience, and consistency, to be identified by oath or ballot with such a political system");<em> id.,</em> at 129 (Covenanters "decline to take any responsible part in the administration of civil power"); W. Gibson &amp; A. McLeod, Reformation Principles Exhibited, by the Reformed Presbyterian Church in the United States of America 138 (1807) ("The juror voluntarily places himself upon oath, under the direction of a law which is immoral.  The Reformed Presbytery declare this practice inconsistent with their Testimony, and warn Church-members against serving on juries under the direction of the constituted courts of law").</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 66" name="FNopinion1.66" href="#FRopinion1.66">66</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See O'Neall, Early History of the Judiciary of South Carolina, p. xi, in 1 Biographical Sketches of the Bench and Bar of South Carolina (1859); Walsh 41-42 (explaining that South Carolina "dismantled" the "five-member constitutional court" that decided <em>Willson</em> and replaced it with a new high court--the South Carolina Court of Appeals--which concurred in the opinion in <em>Farnandis</em>).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 67" name="FNopinion1.67" href="#FRopinion1.67">67</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Hamburger, Religious Exemption 928, and n. 56 (quoting the statement of Rep. Boudinot).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 68" name="FNopinion1.68" href="#FRopinion1.68">68</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Id.,</em> at 928, and n. 57 (quoting the statement of Rep. Benson).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 69" name="FNopinion1.69" href="#FRopinion1.69">69</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Muoz, Original Meaning 1115.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 70" name="FNopinion1.70" href="#FRopinion1.70">70</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Several State Constitutions contained both Free Exercise Clause analogs and provisions protecting conscientious objectors, and this has been cited as evidence that the free-exercise analogs did not confer any right to exemptions.  See <em>id</em>., at 1118-1119.  This argument is unpersuasive for the reasons explained above.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 71" name="FNopinion1.71" href="#FRopinion1.71">71</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;The family name was apparently misspelled in the case caption.  See Sutton, <em>Barnette, </em>Frankfurter, and Judicial Review, 96 Marq. L.&nbsp;Rev. 133, 134 (2012). </p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 72" name="FNopinion1.72" href="#FRopinion1.72">72</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See also N. Feldman, Scorpions 179 (2010).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 73" name="FNopinion1.73" href="#FRopinion1.73">73</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Ibid.</em></p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 74" name="FNopinion1.74" href="#FRopinion1.74">74</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;<em>Id.,</em> at 180.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 75" name="FNopinion1.75" href="#FRopinion1.75">75</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;This discussion does not suggest that <em>Reynolds</em> should be overruled.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 76" name="FNopinion1.76" href="#FRopinion1.76">76</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;"The clear implication was that a 'direct' interference would have been unconstitutional."  McConnell, Free Exercise Revisionism 1125.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 77" name="FNopinion1.77" href="#FRopinion1.77">77</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Our strained attempt to square the ministerial exception with <em>Smith </em>highlights the tension between the two decisions.  <em>Smith</em> held that a generally applicable law satisfies the First Amendment if "prohibiting the exercise of religion .&nbsp;.&nbsp;. is not the object of the [government action] but merely the incidental effect."  494 U.&nbsp;S., at 878.  But the ADA's effect on religion in <em>Hosanna-Tabor</em> was "incidental" in the sense in which the term was used in <em>Smith</em>.  The opinion in <em>Hosanna-Tabor</em> tried to distinguish <em>Smith</em> as involving only "outward physical acts" instead of "the faith and mission of the church itself."  565 U.&nbsp;S., at 190.  But a prohibition of peyote use surely affected "the faith and mission" of the Native American Church, which regards the ingestion of peyote as a sacrament. </p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 78" name="FNopinion1.78" href="#FRopinion1.78">78</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;Recently, some lower courts have proceeded under yet another approach, which analyzes whether the claims presented are sufficiently similar to those raised in the cases that this Court purported to distinguish in <em>Smith</em>.  See <em>Henderson</em> v. <em>McMurray</em>, 987 F. 3d 997, 1006-1007 (CA11 2021); see also <em>Illinois Bible Colleges Assn. </em>v. <em>Anderson</em>, 870 F.&nbsp;3d 631, 641 (CA7 2017).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 79" name="FNopinion1.79" href="#FRopinion1.79">79</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;App. 367-369 (Commissioner Figueora testifying that she was appointed by the mayor, reports ultimately to him, and considers herself part of his administration); Phila. Home Rule Charter, Art. IX, ch. 2, 9-200 (Removal of Appointive Officers).</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 80" name="FNopinion1.80" href="#FRopinion1.80">80</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;App. 182, 365-366.  Apart from the statements made by City officials, other evidence suggested that the City was targeting CSS.  For instance, the City changed its justification for the closure of intake to CSS numerous times.  Brief for Petitioners 12-15 (describing six different justifications).  And although the City's stated harm was that CSS's process for certifying <em>new</em> families was discriminatory, it responded by prohibiting placement with all CSS families, including those already certified.  The City's response therefore appears to "proscribe more religious conduct than is necessary to achieve [its] stated ends."  <em>Lukumi</em>, 508 U.&nbsp;S., at 538.</p>

<br><strong>Footnote <a aria-label="Move to citation 81" name="FNopinion1.81" href="#FRopinion1.81">81</a></strong><br><p>&nbsp;See, <em>e.g.,</em> McConnell, Origins 1409; McConnell, Free Exercise Revisionism 1109; McConnell, Freedom From Persecution 819; Hamburger, Religious Exemption 915; Hamburger, More Is Less 835; Laycock, 7 J. Contemp. Legal Issues 313; Bradley, 20 Hofstra L. Rev. 245; Campbell, A New Approach 973; Kmiec, 59 UMKC L.&nbsp;Rev. 591; Lash, 88 Nw. U. L. Rev. 1106; Lombardi, Free Exercise 369; Muoz, Original Meaning 1083; Nestor 971; Nussbaum, Liberty of Conscience, at 120-130; Walsh 1.</p>

</main><script>_satellite["_runScript1"](function(event, target, Promise) {
_satellite.ads = {};

_satellite.ads.adInfoFactory = function(nameString, href) {
  // TODO remove this once the correct PA is being used for the lid
  if( _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context') && _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context').pa ) {
    nameString = nameString.replace(/pa:[0-9]+/, "pa:"+_satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context').pa);  
  }
  _satellite.logger.debug('_satellite.ads.adInfoFactory nameString: '+nameString);

  // sample name: "&lid=clk:fs/prod:dts/cid:5088127/msa:259/pa:1313/sub:3107462/pos:1"
  var s = nameString;
  s = s.substr(5);
  var lid = s;
  s = s.replaceAll(':','":"');
  s = s.replaceAll('/','","');
  s = '{"'+s+'"}'
  var adInfo = JSON.parse(s);
  adInfo.lid = lid;
  adInfo.paid = (typeof adInfo.sub != 'undefined');
  adInfo.adId = (adInfo.paid ? adInfo.sub : adInfo.cid);
  var map = {
    'ph':'phone',
    'fs':'website',
    'pv':'profile',
    'cu':'contact',
    'vr':'review-read',
    'wr':'review-write',
    'sl':'super-lawyers'
  };  
  adInfo.type = map[adInfo.clk];   
  adInfo.transactionId = _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id')+'-'+adInfo.adId+'-'+(new Date().getTime());
  
  if( href && adInfo.type == 'phone' ) {
    adInfo.detail = href.replace(/[^\d]/g,'');
    if( adInfo.detail.length > 10 ) {
      adInfo.detail = adInfo.detail.substr(adInfo.detail.length-10);
    }
  }  
  
  return adInfo;
}

_satellite.ads.trackAdEngagement = function(adInfo) {
  if( typeof adInfo.adId == 'undefined' ) {
    return false;
  }
  if( typeof FLDataLayer.ads == 'undefined' ) {
    FLDataLayer.ads = {};
  }
  if( typeof FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements == 'undefined' ) {
    FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements = [];
  }
  for( var i=0; i < FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements.length; i++ ) {
    if( FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements[i].type == adInfo.type && FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements[i].adId == adInfo.adId ) {
      return true;
    }
  }

  FLDataLayer.ads.adEngagements.push(adInfo);
  return false;
}

_satellite.ads.sendConversionFindLaw = function() {
  var subId = _satellite.getVar('current_ad_eng').sub;
  var cookieName = 'fl_ad_'+subId;
  var cookieValue = 'true';
  var c = _satellite.cookie.get(cookieName);
  // we use a cookie to ensure multiple beacons are not sent for the same ad
  if( typeof c == 'undefined' ) {
    _satellite.setFlCookie(cookieName, cookieValue, 1);

    var data = {};
    var clickUrlElement = document.getElementById(_satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub'));
    if (clickUrlElement !== null) {
      data.clickUrl = clickUrlElement.innerText;
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context') ) {
      data.adDecisionContext = _satellite.getVar('ad_decision_context');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_transaction_id') ) {
      data.transactionId = _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_transaction_id');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub') ) {
      data.subId = _satellite.getVar('ad_eng_sub');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id') ) {
      data.flUserId = _satellite.getVar('fl_user_id');
    }
    if( _satellite.getVar('fl_tag_track') == 'false' ) {
      data.internalFlag = 'true'; // mimick as an internal request
    }

    let url = new URL(window.location.href);
    let domain = 'attorneys.findlaw'+(_satellite.getVar('cms_env') == 'prod' ? '' : '-stage')+'.com';
    let attorneysUrl = new URL('https://'+domain+'/flstats/v1/stats');
    let searchParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);

    if (searchParams.has('ads-server-env')) {
      attorneysUrl.searchParams.set('ads-server-env', url.searchParams.get('ads-server-env'));
    }
    navigator.sendBeacon(attorneysUrl.href, JSON.stringify(data));
  }
}

      var toStore = type;
      if(type.indexOf("Top-Nav")>-1 || type.indexOf("Next Steps")>-1 ){
        var pageType = _satellite.getVar("page_page_type");
        if(pageType == "article") toStore += " Article";
        if(pageType == "index") toStore += " Index";
      }
      var practiceCode = _satellite.getVar("practice_code");
      if(practiceCode)
        toStore+= "|"+practiceCode
      _satellite.writeCrossSubdomainCookie("s_dsource", toStore);
    };

    _satellite.slowDown = function(e, goTo){
      e.preventDefault(); // prevent default anchor behavior
      setTimeout(function() {
        window.location = goTo;
      }, 300);
    }
    
    //CTA Search - enter & click
    var nextStepsForm = document.querySelector('.nextsteps form');
    nextStepsForm.addEventListener('submit', function(ev) {
      _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Next Steps");
    });

    //Top Nav & Find a Lawyer Page - Enter
    var searchComponent = document.querySelector('#search-component,.hero-content form, .search-secondary form');
    if (searchComponent) {
      searchComponent.addEventListener('keypress', function(e) {
        if (e.key === 'Enter') {
          if (location.host + location.pathname == "lawyers.findlaw.com/")
            _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Find a Lawyer");
          else
            _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Top-Nav");
        }
      });
    }

    //Top Nav & Find a Lawyer Page - click
    var submitButton = document.getElementById('submit-button');
    var heroContentInput = document.querySelector('.hero-content input[type="submit"]');
    var searchSecondaryInput = document.querySelector('.search-secondary input[type="submit"]');
    var submitButtons = [
      submitButton, 
      heroContentInput, 
      searchSecondaryInput
    ];
    for (var i = 0; i < submitButtons.length; i++) {
      var button = submitButtons[i];
      button.addEventListener('click', function(e) {
        if (location.host + location.pathname === "lawyers.findlaw.com/") {
          _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Find a Lawyer");
        } else {
          _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Top-Nav");
        }
      });
    }

    //Homepage search
    if (location.host + location.pathname === "www.findlaw.com/") {
      var forms = document.querySelectorAll("form[action*='stdSearch_process.jsp']");
      for (var i = 0; i < forms.length; i++) {
        var form = forms[i];
        form.addEventListener('submit', function() {
          _satellite.trackSearchSource("Search Box: Home");
        });
      }
    }

    //CTA
    var links = document.querySelectorAll('a[href*="fli="], .articleHeading p a[href*="lawyers.findlaw.com"]');
    for (var i = 0; i < links.length; i++) {
      var link = links[i];
      link.addEventListener('click', function(e) {
        var goTo = link.getAttribute('href');
        _satellite.slowDown(e, goTo);
        var source = link.dataset.searchLocation || '';
        if (!source) {
          if (link.closest('.cta-public').length > 0) {
            source = 'CTA: Banner';
          } else {
            source = 'CTA: Inline Link';
          }
          _satellite.trackSearchSource(source);
        }
      });
    }

    //Right Rail
    var sidebarLawyerSearch = document.querySelectorAll('.sidebarLawyerSearch a[href*="lawyers.findlaw.com"]');
    for (var i = 0; i < sidebarLawyerSearch.length; i++) {
      sidebarLawyerSearch[i].addEventListener('click', function(e) {
        var goTo = this.getAttribute('href');
        _satellite.slowDown(e, goTo);
        _satellite.trackSearchSource("Link Module: Right Rail");
      });
    }

    //Browse
    if (location.host + location.pathname == "lawyers.findlaw.com/") {
      var lawyerLinks = document.querySelectorAll('a[href*="/lawyer"]');
      for (var i = 0; i < lawyerLinks.length; i++) {
        lawyerLinks[i].addEventListener('click', function(e) {
          var goTo = this.getAttribute('href');
          _satellite.slowDown(e, goTo);
          var source = "";
          if (this.getAttribute("href").indexOf("/lawyer/statepractice/") > -1) {
            source = "Browse: Popular Cities";
          } else if (this.getAttribute("href").indexOf("/lawyer/state/") > -1) {
            source = "Browse: State";
          } else if (this.getAttribute("href").indexOf("/lawyer/statecounty/") > -1) {
            source = "Browse: Top Counties";
          } else if (this.getAttribute("href").indexOf("/lawyer/practice/") > -1) {
            source = "Browse: Legal Issue";
          }
          _satellite.trackSearchSource(source);
        });
      }
    }

    //data-search-location
    var linksWithSearchLocation = document.querySelectorAll('[data-search-location] a, a[data-search-location]');
    for (var i = 0; i < linksWithSearchLocation.length; i++) {
      linksWithSearchLocation[i].addEventListener('click', function(e) {
        var goTo = this.getAttribute('href');
        _satellite.slowDown(e, goTo);
        var source = $(this).data("search-location") || $(this).parents("[data-search-location]").data("search-location");
        _satellite.trackSearchSource(source);
      });
    }

  } catch (exp) {
    _satellite.logger.log("Issue with 'Search Source' Rule");
  }
  
});
});</script><script>
function setTrackerCookie(name, value)
{
  var hostParts = location.host.split('.').reverse();
  var cookieDomain = '.' + hostParts[1] + '.' + hostParts[0];
  document.cookie = name + '=' + value + ';domain=' + cookieDomain + ';path=/';
}

setTrackerCookie('fl_last_page_view_id', _satellite.getVar('page_view_id') );
